Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) Trend Analysis Summary

This analysis aims to integrate the latest Manufacturing AI Transformation (AX) trends to identify key trends and challenges. The analysis revealed that many manufacturing sites, including domestic small and medium-sized enterprises, have a high awareness of the necessity of AI adoption. In particular, quality control, production optimization, predictive maintenance, and supply chain optimization are emerging as key application areas for AI.

Key trends significantly emphasize 'AI agent'-based workflow automation for effective processing of manufacturing data and the adoption of the 'Unified Namespace (UNS)' architecture for industrial data standardization. Furthermore, attempts to create new value, such as digitally transferring the know-how of skilled workers or introducing prompt-based design, are also gaining attention.

However, the 'Execution Gap,' stemming from high initial investment costs and a lack of AI technology implementation capabilities, still acts as a major barrier. For a successful AI transformation, it is essential to go beyond simply adopting technology by establishing a systematic data governance strategy and continuously managing AI model performance in response to changing data.

In conclusion, successful manufacturing AX must be pursued based on the establishment of a robust data infrastructure, with clear strategies and long-term investments.

By embedding AI agents within the data pipeline on the manufacturing floor, it's possible to build reliable and scalable operational automation that goes beyond one-time PoCs. The key is to standardize context with industrial knowledge graphs, clarify trust metrics (lineage, quality, explainability, constraint compliance), constantly monitor drift, and apply operational guardrails such as Shadow/Canary deployments. Furthermore, by ensuring interoperability with open standards and existing analytics stacks to avoid vendor lock-in, and through agent fleet orchestration and Human-in-the-loop, safety, quality, and compliance must be guaranteed. In the short term, starting a single embedded workflow pilot, such as for energy optimization or prescriptive maintenance, and establishing a minimal knowledge graph, trust/KPI metrics, drift monitoring, and rollback procedures is a practical starting point.

While 47.4% of domestic small and medium-sized manufacturers recognize the need for AI, initial CAPEX (44.2%) and lack of skilled personnel (20.5%) are barriers. Therefore, lower entry barriers with pilots costing less than 100 million won and subscription/performance-linked models, and pursue a phased AX roadmap with 3-6 month ROI projects such as vision inspection, energy optimization, production scheduling, and predictive maintenance. From the policy and supply side, combine direct subsidies (72.3%) and AI consulting (21.9%), support data collection, standardization, and OEE for early-stage companies, and the proliferation of data platforms and MLOps for advanced companies, managing performance with KPIs (defect rate, MTBF, kWh/Unit, lead time, OEE) to convert the intention to receive government support (54.6%) into actual adoption.

In a survey of 502 domestic small and medium-sized manufacturing companies that have implemented smart factories, 47.4% acknowledged the necessity of AI adoption, and demand increased with higher levels of automation. The biggest barriers were initial investment (44.2%) and labor shortage (20.5%), making low-cost, short-payback pilot projects under 100 million won and two-track support combining government subsidies and consulting effective. Recommended priority use cases include vision inspection, energy optimization, scheduling, and predictive maintenance; early-stage companies should focus on data collection, standardization, and OEE, while advanced companies should concentrate on data platforms, MLOps, and enterprise-wide expansion. Recommended performance KPIs include defect rate, MTBF, kWh/Unit, lead time, and OEE.

MES/ERPÂ·ì„¤ë¹„ ì„¼ì„œ ë°ì´í„° ì •í•©ê³¼ MLOpsë¥¼ ì™¸ë¶€ íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆì™€ ë³‘í–‰ êµ¬ì¶•í•˜ê³ , FTQÂ·OEEÂ·ìŠ¤í¬ë©ë¥ Â·ë¦¬ë“œíƒ€ì„ KPIë¡œ ROIë¥¼ ê³„ëŸ‰í•˜ë©° ì •ë¶€ ë³´ì¡°Â·ë°”ìš°ì²˜(ê´€ì‹¬ 54.6%, ì§ì ‘ì§€ì› í•„ìš” 72.3%)ë¥¼ ì ê·¹ í™œìš©í•˜ì„¸ìš”. The AI adoption priorities for domestic small and medium-sized manufacturers are quality control (33.9%) and production optimization (32.3%). To reduce initial investment (44.2%), which is the biggest barrier, effective strategies include an 8-12 week quality PoC (Proof of Concept) leading to the expansion of successful templates across lines and factories, and reducing TCO (Total Cost of Ownership) through subscription/performance-based contracts. Implement MES/ERP and equipment sensor data integration and MLOps concurrently with external partners, quantify ROI (Return on Investment) using FTQ (First Time Quality), OEE (Overall Equipment Effectiveness), scrap rate, and lead time KPIs (Key Performance Indicators), and actively leverage government subsidies/grants and vouchers (54.6% interested, 72.3% require direct support).

The biggest obstacle is the initial adoption cost, and a lack of expertise and strategy is also a challenge. Practically, an effective approach involves achieving quick results in the quality domain through small-scale PoCs, lowering TCO with cloud and subscription-based models, and complementing data infrastructure and MLOps capabilities with external partners. Actively utilizing direct financial support from the government, and promoting gradual scale-up through KPI-linked ROI management and the dissemination of templates is recommended.

In manufacturing, AI's 'last mile' is substantial due to the absence of data standards and heterogeneous equipment, but incremental value can be generated starting from high-ROI areas like quotation/sourcing, through prompt-based design (with integrated DFM), vision + multi-modal quality inspection, and agent-based workflow automation. Integrate with MES/ERP/PLM using an API-first approach, and control risks by implementing MLOps, governance, and Human-in-the-Loop (HITL) with golden sample/defect catalogs and audit logs, then verify the effectiveness of an 8-12 week pilot using KPIs such as RFQ lead time reduction, FTY improvement, and scrap reduction.

Manufacturing is the 'last mile' of AI adoption, presenting high difficulty, but it offers immediate value in areas such as accelerated quotation and sourcing, prompt-based design, automated quality inspection, and agentic workflows. The key is to view AI not as a tool but as infrastructure, and to establish operational requirements such as CAD/PLM constraint-aware templates and rules, golden sample/defect catalogs, HITL and guardrails, and MES/ERP/PLM API integration. For pilot projects, it is effective to start with high-frequency tasks, validate performance within 8â€“12 weeks using KPIs such as RFQ lead time, FTY, scrap, and throughput, and then expand with a focus on standardization and reusability.

Manufacturing AI has moved from the exploration phase to the operational integration phase. Start with quality inspection (visual inspection) and cybersecurity (anomaly detection and response) where short-term ROI is clear, and drive robotics with a phased roadmap of PoC â†’ Pilot â†’ Field expansion. Success conditions include pre-defined KPIs (FPY, inspection cycle time, scrap/rework costs, security MTTD/MTTR), integration with MES/SCADA/ERP/PLM and OT data, and the establishment of data governance and MLOps systems. Additionally, combine on-site operator participation with retraining, and balance TCO and speed by mixing vendor solutions with in-house development.

AI adoption in manufacturing is moving beyond exploration to the operational internalization phase. Quality inspection and cybersecurity, where short-term performance is clear, are priority application areas, and robotics is presented as the next area of expansion. Success factors are 1) selection of use cases centered on measurable KPIs, 2) integration with MES/OT/IT and establishment of governance and operating systems, and 3) role redesign and reskilling considering on-site resistance. Long-term value comes from inter-technology connectivity, governance, and skilled personnel; therefore, a portfolio-based approach and a phased expansion strategy are effective.

AI should be designed for augmentation, not replacement, and, predicated on human-in-the-loop centered on domain experts and accountable, auditable governance, should pursue small-scale pilots â†’ ROI/OEE verification â†’ scale expansion in areas such as predictive maintenance, schedule optimization, and quality assurance; real value creation is possible by establishing context-rich data governance (data lineage per line, SSOT) and building closed-loop learning that connects production, quality, and equipment data, while simultaneously preparing for agentic workflow orchestration and implementing workforce upskilling and change management.

This study proposes a collaborative mechanism that integrates AI/optimization into the full lifecycle of the supply chain for energy material manufacturing (demand forecasting â€“ procurement â€“ production scheduling â€“ inventory), and by implementing intelligent scheduling through integrating ML/DL-based demand and lead time forecasting with APS, it presents a KPI-level ROI, such as reduced order processing time and improved OTIF, completion rate, and inventory turnover. This study proposes a method to strengthen the supply chain collaboration mechanism in energy material manufacturing with AI. Due to the surge in AI demand, HBM and advanced packaging (2.5D/3D) capabilities have become a bottleneck and a differentiator. The Arizona cluster (TSMC, Intel, Amkor), backed by the CHIPS Act, is accelerating onshoring by lowering lead times, logistics/geopolitical risks, and engineering collaboration costs. From a manufacturing digital transformation (AX) perspective, prioritize the adoption of digital thread/traceability between fab and packaging, AI demand signal-based active capacity planning (linking S&OPâ€“S&OE), process data standardization, and digital twin simulation in the ramp-up phase. Secure resilience with suppliers through localization, joint development, and advance capacity agreements. As human resources are a critical constraint, mitigate yield and utilization risks through upskilling in conjunction with community colleges and apprenticeship programs, along with a standard skill matrix and modular cross-training.

The Ulsan-type 'Sovereign AI' cluster and the strategy to attract a national AI computing center provide a foundation to accelerate high-load manufacturing AI, such as simulation, optimization, and digital twins, in a regional testbed by combining hyperscalers and large-scale computing infrastructure. ERP+AI integration is a transition beyond simple automation to predictive and adaptive intelligence, integrating production, purchasing, finance, sales, service, and supply chain data to implement execution recommendations and trigger-based automation; prioritize the application of material shortage prediction + automatic ordering, predictive maintenance scheduling, and constraint-based dynamic scheduling; and after establishing human-centric governance, such as approval thresholds and exception management, self-learning loops utilizing plan-performance/on-site feedback, and a data foundation including master data consistency and OT/IoT streaming, operationalize it with a 90-day pilot and MLOps within the ERP, then verify its effectiveness with KPIs such as OTD, inventory turnover, schedule adherence, MTBF/MTTR.

Applying AI to manufacturing contracts (MPA/MSA, manufacturing, supply, distribution) can shorten review time by up to 85% through automatic clause detection, risk ranking, and standardization of playbooks (Must/Nice/Fallback). PLM monetization is shifting from large-scale customized implementations to productized services, integrated middleware, AI Copilot, Micro-SaaS, and analytics/training. This strongly aligns with the 'rapid pilot - iterative value creation - subscription-based operation' model of manufacturing AX, particularly when a digital thread connecting data-people-processes is established. Manufacturers should adopt lightweight connectors between PLM-ERP-MES-CAD, pilot AI Copilot in change management (ECR/ECO) workflows to measure KPIs such as lead time, rework, and approval cycles, and prioritize data governance, including master data, attribute standardization, and version/status management. For vendors/partners, it is effective to lower entry barriers and build repeatable revenue models by combining Micro-SaaS specialized in micro-domains such as specification document generation, part similarity search, and change impact summarization, with accelerators/templates.

This article points out that how money is made in PLM in 2025 is shifting from a focus on large-scale implementations to productized services, integration, AI copilot, micro SaaS, and analytics, education, and content. From a manufacturing perspective, premised on a digital thread (connecting data-people-processes), it is practical that rapid value creation is possible through methods such as (1) implementing PLM-ERP-MES-CAD integration accelerators, (2) pilot application of AI copilot for change management and BOM impact analysis, (3) strengthening PLM data governance, (4) operating engineering analytics dashboards, and (5) internal productization of education/content. Sinequa for Manufacturing offers a knowledge infrastructure that can boost productivity, reduce errors, speed up maintenance, and increase design reuse by connecting distributed manufacturing data from PLM, ERP, CAD, MRO, and other systems with semantic search and RAG. However, due to its strong promotional nature, specific examples/figures are lacking, therefore, an approach that quickly verifies the tangible effects with internal data through a pilot is suitable.

íœ´ë¨¸ë…¸ì´ë“œ ë¡œë´‡ì€ ë¸Œë¼ìš´í•„ë“œ ê³µì¥ì—ì„œ ë¼ì¸ í”¼ë”©Â·í‚¤íŒ…Â·ìì¬ ì´ì†¡ ë“± ê³ ë³€ë™Â·ê³ ë¹ˆë„ ë³€ê²½ ì‘ì—…ì„ ê¸°ì¡´ ì„¤ë¹„ì™€ ë™í˜•ìœ¼ë¡œ ëŒ€ì²´/ë³´ì™„í•´ ì¸ë ¥ ë¶€ì¡± ì™„í™”ì™€ ìƒì‚°ì„± í–¥ìƒì„ ë™ì‹œì— ë…¸ë¦´ ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë©°, ì¸ê°„í˜• í¼íŒ©í„°ë¡œ í†µí•© ì¥ë²½ì´ ë‚®ìŠµë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¯¸Â·ì¤‘ ê²½ìŸê³¼ ì¤‘êµ­ í˜ì‹ ì„¼í„°ì˜ í˜„ì¥ ë°ì´í„° ì„ ìˆœí™˜ ì „ëµì„ ê°ì•ˆí•´, ì œì¡°ì‚¬ëŠ” ì €ìœ„í—˜ ë°˜ë³µì—…ë¬´ë¶€í„° ë‹¨ê³„ì  íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ì„ ì‹¤í–‰í•˜ê³  KPI(MTBF, ì‘ì—… ì„±ê³µë¥ , ì‚¬ì´í´íƒ€ì„ í¸ì°¨, ë‹¨ìœ„ ì‘ì—…ë¹„ìš©)ë¥¼ ëª…í™•í™”í•˜ë©° ì•ˆì „Â·ë ˆì´ì•„ì›ƒ(ISO 10218/TS 15066) ê²€ì¦ê³¼ ì¸í”„ë¼(í”Œë¦¿ ê´€ë¦¬, ë°°í„°ë¦¬/ì¶©ì „, 5G/Wiâ€‘Fi, ì—£ì§€Â·ë°ì´í„° íŒŒì´í”„ë¼ì¸/ë””ì§€í„¸ íŠ¸ìœˆ)ë¥¼ ë³‘í–‰í•˜ê³ , íŒŒíŠ¸ë„ˆì‹­ìœ¼ë¡œ ìì‚¬ ê³µì • ë°ì´í„°ì…‹ì„ í™•ë³´í•´ì•¼ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. ë¹„ìš© í•˜ë½ ê°€ì†ìœ¼ë¡œ 12~24ê°œì›” ë‚´ ì¼ë¶€ ì‘ì—…ì—ì„œ ì‚¬ì—…ì„±ì´ ì—´ë¦´ ìˆ˜ ìˆìœ¼ë¯€ë¡œ, ì„ ì œì  íŒŒì¼ëŸ¿ ì˜ˆì‚°Â·ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤ì™€ ìŠ¤ì¼€ì¼ì—… ê³„íšì„ ë§ˆë ¨í•˜ì‹­ì‹œì˜¤. Humanoid robots in brownfield factories can simultaneously aim to alleviate labor shortages and improve productivity by replacing/complementing high-variability, high-frequency change operations like line feeding, kitting, and material transfer in a manner analogous to existing equipment, and they have low integration barriers due to their human-like form factor. Considering U.S.-China competition and China's innovation centers' on-site data virtuous cycle strategy, manufacturers should execute phased pilots starting with low-risk repetitive tasks, clarify KPIs (MTBF, task success rate, cycle time deviation, unit task cost), conduct safety and layout (ISO 10218/TS 15066) verification in parallel with infrastructure (fleet management, battery/charging, 5G/Wi-Fi, edge/data pipeline/digital twin), and secure their own process datasets through partnerships. With accelerating cost reductions, business viability may emerge for some tasks within 12-24 months; therefore, prepare proactive pilot budgets, governance, and scale-up plans.

The core of manufacturing AX transformation is establishing an integrated framework (Central+CORBI) that achieves single visibility by standardizing and refining distributed data from sources such as IoT, MES, ERP, CRM, and WMS using no-code iPaaS, and then leveraging this to connect predictive insights and business automation. For practical application, it is possible to transition from reactive to proactive operations by first implementing data source inventorying, common data model/master data maintenance, event-driven (real-time/near real-time) integration, and data governance/quality indicator operations, and then prioritizing the application of virtual assistant-type AI for work instruction confirmation, inventory inquiry, quality issue summarization, and reporting automation.

This document presents a maturity roadmap (Reactive â†’ Intelligent â†’ Autonomous/4 stages) and core building blocks (Inference, Planning, Orchestration, Collaboration, Learning) for applying AIOps and Agentic AI to manufacturing IT/OT operations, which can be directly utilized for establishing Smart Factory operational strategies. ë³¸ ì—°êµ¬ëŠ” ì œì¡° AXì—ì„œ AI ê¸°ë°˜ ì˜ì‚¬ê²°ì •ì§€ì›ì˜ ì„±ê³¼ë¥¼ ì¢Œìš°í•˜ëŠ” â€˜ë°ì´í„° ìˆ˜ì§‘Â·í†µí•©(DCI)â€™ì„ í•µì‹¬ ê¸°ë°˜ìœ¼ë¡œ ì œì‹œí•˜ë©°, OT/IT í‘œì¤€í™”Â·ë°ì´í„° í’ˆì§ˆ/ê±°ë²„ë„ŒìŠ¤Â·ë©”íƒ€ë°ì´í„° ì •ë¹„ê°€ ì˜ˆì¸¡ë¶„ì„ê³¼ ì‹¤ì‹œê°„ DSSì˜ í•„ìˆ˜ ì „ì œì„ì„ ëª…í™•íˆ í•©ë‹ˆë‹¤. Since the concurrent boom in HBM and commodity DRAM, along with packaging bottlenecks, will increase the lead time and price volatility of AI servers and edge hardware, manufacturers must concurrently finalize IT/OT budgets early, implement phased expansion (Phase-in), and redesign memory Long-Term Agreements (LTA), dual sourcing, and safety stock. Bio-inspired optimization, such as Slime Mould and Ant Colony Optimization, can be directly utilized for decision-making in manufacturing supply chains and internal logistics (inter-plant transportation networks, milk runs, warehouse picking, AGV/AMR routes) that simultaneously considers cost, time, carbon, and risk. By adopting 'Green Premium' as a decision-making framework, prioritize projects that can lower the abatement cost per ton. Improve process efficiency, yield, and energy intensity using AI/automation and digital twin to simultaneously reduce costs and emissions. Establish real-time MRV linked with MES/EMS and product-level carbon footprints, and deploy an innovation pipeline from pilot to scale, including electrification of high-heat processes (electric heating/heat pumps), fuel switching (green hydrogen, biogas), CCUS, and the utilization of renewable energy and storage systems. Just as recent innovations have significantly lowered emissions projections, you can rapidly reduce the Green Premium and strengthen competitiveness through early investment and supply chain Scope 3 data linkage.

The core of the article is that the solution to the climate crisis depends on 'technological innovation' and the reduction of the green premium. From a manufacturing perspective, practical action points include improving process energy efficiency and yield by utilizing AI and automation, and establishing pilot and scale strategies for low-carbon technologies such as electrification, fuel switching, and CCUS. By establishing a real-time emission data infrastructure linked with MES/EMS and internal carbon pricing to set investment priorities based on abatement cost per ton, and by performing process redesign and investment feasibility verification with digital twins, the green premium can be progressively reduced. This aligns with the direction of manufacturing AX (data-driven, simulation & optimization, supply chain linkage).

The APEC 'Incheon Plan' and the AI and digital transformation agenda are expected to lead data utilization, trustworthy AI governance, and supply chain digitalization standards over the next 5 years, and in conjunction with the domestic '7 Major Physical AI Projects (Physical AI),' will support the spread of robotics, edge AI, and autonomation in manufacturing sites. Manufacturing companies should reflect this in their mid-to-long-term roadmaps, prioritize high value-added process automation, AI-assisted decision-making, and up- and re-skilling, and proactively explore pilot projects and joint research utilizing APEC cooperation tracks, along with the linkage of funding and tax incentives. Simultaneously, mitigate supply chain risks by concurrently implementing talent strategies to address aging populations and labor shortages and monitoring global standard changes.

The APEC Finance and Structural Reform Ministerial Meeting suggests that the proliferation of AI, changes in industrial structure, productivity transformation, and responses to demographic shifts will become the core pillars of regional policy cooperation over the next five years. Korea's '7 Major Physical AI Projects' and AI talent development plan indicate the possibility of policy support for automation and autonomy in manufacturing sites. It is effective for manufacturers to proactively prepare an AI investment roadmap tailored to the Incheon Plan, address data, standards, and governance, implement upskilling programs, and tackle supply chain digitalization challenges, while also exploring opportunities to participate in APEC cooperation programs (pilot projects, joint research, incentives).
